\(\sqrt[n]{\dfrac{a}{b}} = \dfrac{\sqrt[n]{a}}{\sqrt[n]{b}}\)

\(\sqrt[n]{a} \times \sqrt[n]{b} = \sqrt[n]{ab}\)
----
\(\sqrt[n]{\dfrac{a}{b}} = \dfrac{\sqrt[n]{a}}{\sqrt[n]{b}}\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		    \sqrt[n]{a} \times \sqrt[n]{b}
		    &= a^{\frac{1}{n}} \times b^{\frac{1}{n}} \\
		    &= (ab)^{\frac{1}{n}} \\
		    &= \sqrt[n]{ab}
		    \end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		    \sqrt[n]{\frac{a}{b}}
		    &= \left( \frac{a}{b} \right)^{\frac{1}{n}} \\
		    &= \dfrac{a^{\frac{1}{n}}}{b^{\frac{1}{n}}} \\
		    &= \dfrac{\sqrt[n]{a}}{\sqrt[n]{b}}
		    \end{align}\]

\(z - 4\sqrt{z} + 3 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{align} 
		  z - 4\sqrt{z} + 3   &= 0 \\ 			
		  z - 4z^{\frac{1}{2}} + 3   &= 0 \\
		  (z^{\frac{1}{2}}-3)(z^{\frac{1}{2}}-1)   &= 0
		  \end{align}\]
----
\(a \times b = 0\)
----
\(a = 0\)
----
\(b = 0\)
----
\[\therefore (z^{\frac{1}{2}}-3) = 0 \text{ or } (z^{\frac{1}{2}}-1) = 0\]
----
\[\begin{align}  			
		  z^{\frac{1}{2}}-3 &= 0 \\
		  z^{\frac{1}{2}}   &= 3 \\
		  \left( z^{\frac{1}{2}} \right)^2 &= 3^2 \\
		  z &= 9 
		  \end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}  			
		  z^{\frac{1}{2}}-1 &= 0 \\
		  z^{\frac{1}{2}}   &= 1 \\
		  \left( z^{\frac{1}{2}} \right)^2 &= 1^2 \\
		  z &= 1
		  \end{align}\]
----
\(z=9\)
----
\[\begin{align}  			
		  \text{LHS}&= z - 4\sqrt{z} + 3   \\
		  &= 9 - 4\sqrt{9} + 3    \\
		  &= 12 - 12   \\
		  &=  0   \\
		  &=\text{RHS }
		  \end{align}\]
----
\(z=1\)
----
\[\begin{align}  			
		  \text{LHS} &= z - 4\sqrt{z} + 3   \\
		  &= 1 - 4\sqrt{1} + 3  \\
		  &= 4-4  \\
		  &=  0   \\
		  &= \text{RHS }
		  \end{align}\]
----
\(z - 4\sqrt{z} + 3 = 0\)
----
\(z = 9\)
----
\(z = 1\)

		  \left( \sqrt{p-2} \right)^2 &= 3^2 \\

		  \text{LHS} &=\sqrt{p-2} - 3   \\
		  &=\sqrt{11-2} - 3  \\
		  &=\sqrt{9} - 3  \\
		  &= 3-3   \\
		  &= 0   \\
		  &= \text{RHS }

\(2^{x+1} -32 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
2^{x+1}-32&=0 \\
2^{x+1}&=32 \\
2^{x+1}&=2^5 \\
\therefore x+1&=5 \\
x&=4
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(x = 4\)
----
\(p = 3\)
----
\(2y^{\frac{1}{2}} - 3y^{\frac{1}{4}} + 1 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
2y^{\frac{1}{2}}-3y^{\frac{1}{4}}+1&=0 \\
\left ( 2y^\frac{1}{4} -1\right )\left ( y^\frac{1}{4} -1\right )&=0 \\
\text{Therefore } 2y^{\frac{1}{4}}-1&=0  \\
y^{\frac{1}{4}}-\frac{1}{2}&=0 \\
y^\frac{1}{4}&=\frac{1}{2} \\
y^\frac{4}{4} &= \left ( \frac{1}{2} \right )^4 \\
\therefore y&=\frac{1}{16} \\
\text{or} \\
y^\frac{1}{4}-1&=0 \\
y^\frac{1}{4}&=1 \\
\therefore y&=1
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(y = 1\)
----
\(t-1 = \sqrt{7-t}\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
t-1 &= \sqrt{7-t} \\
\left ( t-1 \right )^2 &= \left ( \sqrt{7-t} \right )^2 \\
t^2 - 2t + 1 &=  7-t  \\
t^2 - t - 6 &=0 \\
(t - 3)(t + 2)&= 0 \\
\therefore  t =3  &\text{ or } t = - 2 \\
\text{Check RHS for } t = 3:  &= \sqrt{7-3} \\
   						&= \sqrt{4} \\
   						&= 2 \\
   						&= \text{LHS} \therefore \text{ valid solution }\\
\text{Check RHS for } t = -2:  &= \sqrt{7-(-2)} \\
   						&= \sqrt{9} \\
   						&= 3 \\
   						&\ne \text{LHS} \therefore \text{ not valid solution } 
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(t = 3\)
----
\(2z - 7\sqrt{z} + 3 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
2z-7z^\frac{1}{2}+3&=0 \\
\left ( z^\frac{1}{2}-3 \right )\left ( 2z^\frac{1}{2}-1 \right )&=0 \\
\text{Therefore } z^\frac{1}{2}-3&=0 \\
\left ( z^\frac{1}{2} \right )^2 &=3^2 \\
\therefore z&=9 \\
\text{or}\\
2z^\frac{1}{2}-1&=0 \\
\left ( z^\frac{1}{2} \right )^2&=\left ( \frac{1}{2} \right )^2 \\
\therefore z&=\frac{1}{4}
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(z = 9\)
----
\(z = \frac{1}{4}\)
----
\(x^{\frac{1}{3}}(x^{\frac{1}{3}} + 1) = 6\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
x^\frac{1}{3}\left ( x^\frac{1}{3}+1 \right )&=6 \\
x^\frac{2}{3}+x^\frac{1}{3} &=6 \\
\left ( x^\frac{1}{3}-2 \right )\left ( x^\frac{1}{3}+3 \right ) &= 0 \\
\text{Therefore } x^\frac{1}{3}-2 &= 0 \\
x^\frac{1}{3} &= 2 \\
\therefore x&=8 \\
\text{or} \\
x^\frac{1}{3}+3 &= 0 \\
x^\frac{1}{3} &=-3 \\
\therefore x &= -27
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(x = 8\)
----
\(x = -27\)
----
\(2^{4n} - \dfrac{1}{\sqrt[4]{16}} = 0\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
2^{4n}-\dfrac{1}{\sqrt[4]{16}}&=0\\
2^{4n}&=\dfrac{1}{16^\frac{1}{4}} \\
2^{4n}&=\dfrac{1}{\left (2^4  \right )^\frac{1}{4}} \\
2^{4n}&=\frac{1}{2} \\
2^{4n}&=2^{-1} \\
\therefore 4n&=-1 \\
\therefore n &=-\frac{1}{4}
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(n = -\frac{1}{4}\)
----
\(\sqrt{31 -10d} = 4 - d\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{31-10d}&=d-4 \\
\left (\sqrt{31-10d}  \right )^2&=\left (d-4  \right )^2 \\
31-10d&=d^2-8d+16 \\
0&=d^2+2d-15 \\
0&=\left ( d-3 \right )\left ( d+5 \right ) \\ 
\text{Therefore } d&= 3 \\
\text{or} \\
d&= -5 \\
\text{Check LHS for } d = 3:  &= \sqrt{31 - 30} \\
   						&= \sqrt{1} \\
   						&= 1 \\
   						&= \text{RHS} \therefore \text{ valid solution }\\
\text{Check LHS for } t = -5:  &= \sqrt{31-(-50)} \\
   						&= \sqrt{81} \\
   						&= 9 \\
   						&= \text{RHS} \therefore \text{ valid solution }
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(d = 3\)
----
\(d = -5\)
----
\(y - 10\sqrt{y} + 9 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
y - 10\sqrt{y} + 9 &= 0  \\
y - 10y^{\frac{1}{2}} + 9 &= 0  \\
\left( y^{\frac{1}{2}} - 1  \right ) \left( y^{\frac{1}{2}} -9 \right )  &= 0 \\
\text{Therefore } y^{\frac{1}{2}} - 1  &= 0 \\
y^{\frac{1}{2}}  &= 1 \\
\left( y^{\frac{1}{2}} \right )^2 &= (1)^2 \\
\therefore y  &= 1 \\
\text{or} \\
y^{\frac{1}{2}} - 9 & = 0  \\
y^{\frac{1}{2}}  &= 9 \\
\left( y^{\frac{1}{2}} \right )^2 &= (9)^2 \\
\therefore y  &= 81 
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(y = 1\)
----
\(y = 81\)
----
\(f = 2 + \sqrt{19 - 2f}\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
f &= 2 + \sqrt{19 - 2f} \\
f - 2 &=   \sqrt{19 - 2f} \\
\left( f - 2 \right )^2 &=   \left( \sqrt{19 - 2f} \right )^2  \\
f^2 - 4f + 4 &= 19 - 2f  \\
 f^2 - 2f -15  &= 0 \\
(f - 5)(f + 3)  &= 0 \\
\text{Therefore } f - 5  &= 0 \\
\therefore f  &= 5 \\
\text{or} \\
f + 3  & = 0  \\
\therefore f  &= -3 \\
\text{Check RHS for } f = 5:  &= 2 + \sqrt{19 - 10} \\
   						&= 2 + \sqrt{9} \\
   						&= 5 \\
   						&= \text{LHS} \therefore \text{ valid solution }\\
\text{Check RHS for } f = -3:  &= 2 + \sqrt{19 + 6}\\
   						&= 2 + \sqrt{25} \\
   						&= 7 \\
   						&\ne \text{LHS} \therefore \text{ not valid solution }
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(f = 5\)

\(2x^{\frac{2}{3}} + 3x^{\frac{1}{3}} - 2 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	2x^{\frac{2}{3}} + 3x^{\frac{1}{3}} - 2 &= 0 \\
	\left( 2x^{\frac{1}{3}} - 1  \right) \left( x^{\frac{1}{3}}  + 2  \right) &= 0 \\
		\therefore 2x^{\frac{1}{3}} - 1 &= 0 \\
		2x^{\frac{1}{3}}	&= 1 \\
		x^{\frac{1}{3}}	&= \frac{1}{2} \\
		\left( x^{\frac{1}{3}} \right)^3	&= \left( \frac{1}{2} \right)^3 \\
		\therefore x	&= \frac{1}{8}  \\
		\text{ or } &  \\ 
 	 x^{\frac{1}{3}}  + 2  &=  0 \\ 
 	 x^{\frac{1}{3}}   &=  -2 \\ 
 	\left( x^{\frac{1}{3}} \right)^3  &= \left( -2 \right)^3 \\ 
 	 x  &= -8 \\ 
 \text{Therefore } x = \frac{1}{8} &\text{ or } x = -8  
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(x = \frac{1}{8} \text{ or } x = -8\)

\(\sqrt{\dfrac{3^{x+1} - 3^x}{3^{x-1}} + 3}\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
 \text{LHS }  &= \sqrt{\dfrac{3^{x+1} - 3^x}{3^{x-1}} + 3} \\
				&=  \sqrt{\dfrac{3^{x+1}}{3^{x-1}} - \dfrac{3^{x}}{3^{x-1}}+ 3} \\
				&=  \sqrt{3^{x+1-x+1} -  3^{x-x+1} + 3} \\
				&=  \sqrt{3^{2} -  3^{1} + 3} \\
				&=  \sqrt{3^{2}} \\
				&=  3 \\
				&=   \text{RHS }
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(\sqrt{\dfrac{3^{x+1} - 3^x}{3^{x-1}} + 3} = \left( \dfrac{1}{3} \right)^{x-2}\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
 \sqrt{\dfrac{3^{x+1} - 3^x}{3^{x-1}} + 3} &=  \left( \dfrac{1}{3} \right)^{x-2} \\
 3  &=  \left( \frac{1}{3} \right)^{x-2} \\
 3  &=  \left( 3\right)^{-x+2} \\
		1		&=  -x + 2\\
		x		&=  1
\end{aligned}\]
----
\(x = 1\)

\(\sqrt{5-2p} - 4 = \frac{1}{2}p\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		  \sqrt{5-2p} - 4  &= \frac{1}{2}p \\
		  \sqrt{5-2p}  &= \frac{1}{2}p + 4 \\
		  \left( \sqrt{5-2p} \right) ^2  &= \left( \frac{1}{2}p + 4 \right)^2 \\
		  5-2p   &=   \frac{p^2}{4} + 4p +16   \\
		  0   &=   \frac{p^2}{4} + 6p + 11   \\
		  0   &=   p^2 + 24p + 44   \\

  &=\dfrac{-1 \pm \sqrt{49}}{6}\\
  &=\dfrac{-1 \pm 7}{6}\\
  t = \dfrac{-1+7}{6}= \frac{6}{6}=1 &\text{ or } t = \dfrac{-1-7}{6}=\frac{-8}{6} = \frac{-4}{3}
\end{align}\]

\(-25{y}^{2}+25y-4=0\)
----
\[\begin{align}
  -25y^2 + 25y - 4 &= 0\\
  25y^2 - 25y+4 &= 0\\
  y^2 - y &= -\frac{4}{25}\\
  y^2 - y + \frac{1}{4} &= -\frac{4}{25} + \frac{1}{4}\\
  \left(y-\frac{1}{2}\right)^2 &= \frac{-16+25}{100}\\
  \left(y-\frac{1}{2}\right)^2 &= \frac{9}{100}\\
  y-\frac{1}{2} &= \pm \sqrt{\frac{9}{100}}\\
  y-\frac{1}{2} &= \pm \frac{3}{10}\\
  y = \frac{1}{2}+\frac{3}{10} = \frac{4}{5} &\text{ or } y = \frac{1}{2} - \frac{3}{10} = \frac{1}{5}
\end{align}\]

\({y}^{2}+3+\dfrac{12}{{y}^{2}+3}=7\)

		\text{Let } y^2+3&=k\\
		\text{Restriction: } y^2+3&\ne 0 \\
		\text{Therefore } k &\ne 0 \\
		\therefore k + \frac{12}{k} &= 7\\
		k^2 + 12 &= 7k\\
		k^2 - 7k + 12 &= 0\\
		(k-3)(k-4) &= 0\\
		k=3 &\text{ or } k=4\\
		\therefore y^2 + 3 =3 &\text{ or } y^2 + 3 = 4\\
		\therefore y^2 =0 &\text{ or }  y^2 = 1\\
		\therefore y=0 &\text{ or } y= \pm 1
		\end{align}\]

\(2x^2 + x - 3 = 0\)
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
  		ax^2 + bx + c &= 0 & \\[8pt]
		a + \dfrac{b}{x} + \dfrac{c}{x^2} &= 0 & \text{Divided by } x^2 \text{ where } x\ne 0 \\[8pt]
		\dfrac{c}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{x} + a &= 0 & \text{Rearranged} \\[8pt]
		\dfrac{1}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{cx} + \dfrac{a}{c} &= 0 & \text{Divided by } c \text{ where } c \ne 0 \\[8pt]
		\dfrac{1}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{cx} &= -\dfrac{a}{c} & \text{Subtracted } \frac{a}{c} \text{ from both sides} \\[8pt]
		\therefore \dfrac{1}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{cx} + \dots & & \text{Got stuck}
		\end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
  		x =& \dfrac{2c}{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}\\
		&= \dfrac{2(-3)}{-(1) \pm \sqrt{1^2 - 4(2)(-3)}}\\
		&=\dfrac{-6}{-1 \pm \sqrt{25}}\\
		&= \dfrac{-6}{-1 \pm 5}\\
		x = \frac{-6}{4} = -\frac{3}{2} & \text{ or } x = \frac{-6}{-6} = 1
		\end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
  		2x^2 + x -3 &= 0\\
		(2x+3)(x-1)&=0\\
		x = -\frac{3}{2}& \text{ or } x=1
		\end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
  		ax^2 + bx + c &= 0 \\
		a + \dfrac{b}{x} + \dfrac{c}{x^2} &= 0 \\
		\dfrac{c}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{x} + a &= 0 \\
		\dfrac{1}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{cx} + \dfrac{a}{c} &= 0 \\
		\dfrac{1}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{cx} &= -\dfrac{a}{c} \\
		\dfrac{1}{x^2} + \dfrac{b}{cx} + \dfrac{b^2}{4c^2} &= -\dfrac{a}{c} +\dfrac{b^2}{4c^2}\\
		\left(\dfrac{1}{x} + \dfrac{b}{2c}\right)^2 &= \dfrac{-4ac +b^2}{4c^2}  = \dfrac{b^2-4ac}{4c^2}\\
		\dfrac{1}{x} + \dfrac{b}{2c} &= \pm \sqrt{\dfrac{b^2-4ac}{4c^2}}\\
		\dfrac{1}{x} &= - \dfrac{b}{2c} \pm \sqrt{\dfrac{b^2-4ac}{4c^2}}\\
		\dfrac{1}{x} &= \dfrac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2c}\\
		\therefore x &= \dfrac{2c}{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}
		\end{align}\]

\(T_n = an^2 + bn + c\)

\[\begin{align}
		n=1:  T_1 &= a + b + c \\
		n=2:  T_2 &= 4a + 2b + c \\
		n=3:   T_3 &= 9a + 3b + c
		\end{align}\]

\(a\)

\(b\)

\(c\)
----
\(T_1 = 5\)
----
\(T_2 = 12\)
----
\(T_3 = 23\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		a + b + c  &= 5 \\
		4a + 2b + c  &= 12 \\
		9a + 3b + c  &= 23
		\end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
		T_2 - T_1 &= 4a + 2b + c - (a + b + c) & \\
		12 - 5	  &= 4a + 2b + c - a - b - c   & \\
		7	  &= 3a + b                    & \ldots (1)
		\end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
		T_3 - T_2  &= 9a + 3b + c - (4a + 2b + c) & \\
		23 - 12    &=  9a + 3b + c - 4a - 2b - c  & \\
		11         &=  5a + b                     & \ldots (2)
		\end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		(2)-(1)  &= 5a + b - (3a + b) \\
		11 - 7 &= 5a + b - 3a - b \\
		4 &= 2a \\
		\therefore a &= 2
		\end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		\text{Using equation } (1): \quad 3(2) + b &= 7 \\
		\therefore b &= 1 \\
		\text{And using } \quad a + b + c 		 &= 5 \\
		  2 + 1 + c 		 &= 5 \\
		\therefore c &= 1
		\end{align}\]

\(T_n = an^2 + bn + c\)
----
\(T_n\)
----
\(a\)
----
\(b\)
----
\(c\)
----
\(T_n = an^2 + bn + c\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		n=1:  T_1 &= a + b + c \\
		n=2:  T_2 &= 4a + 2b + c \\
		n=3:   T_3 &= 9a + 3b + c
		\end{align}\]
----
\(a\)
----
\(b\)
----
\(c\)
----
\(T_1 = 3\)
----
\(T_2 = 6\)
----
\(T_3 = 10\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		a + b + c  &= 3 \\
		4a + 2b + c  &= 6 \\
		9a + 3b + c  &= 10
		\end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
		T_2 - T_1  &= 4a + 2b + c - (a + b + c) \\
		6 - 3	   &= 4a + 2b + c - a - b - c  \\
		3	   &= 3a + b  & \ldots (1)
		\end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
		T_3 - T_2  &= 9a + 3b + c - (4a + 2b + c) \\
		10 - 6  &=  9a + 3b + c - 4a - 2b - c  \\
		4  &=  5a + b  & \ldots (2)
		\end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		(2)-(1)  &= 5a + b - (3a + b) \\
		4 - 3 &= 5a + b - 3a - b \\
		1 &= 2a \\
		\therefore a &= \frac{1}{2}
		\end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		\text{Using equation }(1): \quad  3\left(\frac{1}{2}\right) + b &= 3 \\
		\therefore b &= \frac{3}{2} \\
		\text{And using } \quad a + b + c 		 &= 3 \\
		\frac{1}{2} + \frac{3}{2} + c 		 &= 3 \\
		\therefore c &= 1
		\end{align}\]
----
\(T_n = \frac{1}{2}n^2 + \frac{3}{2}n + 1\)

\(T_n = an^2 + bn + c\)
----
\(T_n\)
----
\(a\)
----
\(b\)
----
\(c\)
----
\(T_n = an^2 + bn + c\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		  n=1:  T_1 &= a + b + c \\
		  n=2:  T_2 &= 4a + 2b + c \\
		  n=3:   T_3 &= 9a + 3b + c
		  \end{align}\]
----
\(a\)
----
\(b\)
----
\(c\)
----
\(T_1 = 6\)
----
\(T_2 = 10\)
----
\(T_3 = 15\)
----
\[\begin{align}
		  a + b + c  &= 6 \\
		  4a + 2b + c  &= 10 \\
		  9a + 3b + c  &= 15
		  \end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
		  T_2 - T_1  &= 4a + 2b + c - (a + b + c) \\
		  10 - 6	 &= 4a + 2b + c - a - b - c  \\
		  4	 &= 3a + b  & \ldots (1)
		  \end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{alignrll}
		  T_3 - T_2  &= 9a + 3b + c - (4a + 2b + c) \\
		  15- 10  &=  9a + 3b + c - 4a - 2b - c  \\
		  5  &=  5a + b  & \ldots (2)
		  \end{alignrll}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		  (2)-(1)  &= 5a + b - (3a + b) \\
		  5-4 &= 5a + b - 3a - b \\
		  1 &= 2a \\
		  \therefore a &= \frac{1}{2}
		  \end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
		  \text{Using equation } (1): \quad  3\left(\frac{1}{2}\right) + b &= 4 \\
		  \therefore b &= \frac{5}{2} \\
									\text{And using } a + b + c 		 &= 6 \\
		  \frac{1}{2} + \frac{5}{2} + c 		 &= 6 \\
		  \therefore c &= 3
		  \end{align}\]
----
\(T_n = \frac{1}{2}n^2 + \frac{5}{2}n + 3\)

\(T_n = 5n^2 + 3n + 4\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	T_n &= 5n^2 + 3n + 4  \\
	T_1 &= 5(1)^2 + 3(1) + 4  \\
	    &= 12 \\
	T_2 &= 5(2)^2 + 3(2) + 4  \\
	    &= 30 \\
	T_3 &= 5(3)^2 + 3(3) + 4  \\
	    &= 58 \\
	T_4 &= 5(4)^2 + 3(4) + 4  \\
	    &= 96 \\
	T_5 &= 5(5)^2 + 3(5) + 4  \\
	    &= 144 
	\end{aligned}\]

\(12;30;58;96;144\)

 4 &= n

\(16; 27; 42; 61; \ldots\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	\text{Second difference: } &= 4 \\
	\text{First differences: } &=  11;15;19;23;27 \\
 	\therefore T_5 &=  61+23  \\
 								&= 84   \\
 	\therefore T_6 &= 84 +27   \\
 								&= 111
	\end{aligned}\]

----
\[\begin{aligned}
	T_n &= an^2 +bn +c  \\
	T_1 &= a +b +c  \\
	T_2 &= 4n^2 +2n +c  \\
	T_3 &= 9n^2 +3n +c 
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	\therefore a + b+ c &= 16  \\
	 \therefore c &=  16 - a - b \\
	 4a + 2b + c    &= 27 \\
	 4a + 2b + (16 - a - b)    &= 27 \\
	 3a + b     &= 11 \\
	\text{And } 9a + 3b + c &= 42 \\
 \therefore 9a + 3b + (16 - a - b) &= 42 \\
	8a + 2b = 26 \\
	4a + b =  13 \\
	\therefore b &= 13 -4a
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	\therefore 3a + b &= 11 \\
	3a + (13 - 4a) &= 11 \\
	-a  &= -2 \\
	\therefore a  &=  2 \\
	b  &=  13 -4(2) \\
	\therefore b &= 5 \\
  \text{And } c  &= 16 - a - b \\
  \therefore c  &= 16 - 2 -5 \\
			 &= 9 \\
	\therefore T_n  &= 2n^2 + 5n + 9
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\(T_n = 2n^2 + 5n + 9\)

\[\begin{aligned}
	T_n &=  an^2 + bn + c \\
	\text{Second difference: } 2a &= 2 \\
														\therefore a &= 1 \\
	3a + b  &=  3 \\
 	b &=  3 - 3(1)  \\
 					\therefore b &= 0   \\
 	a + b + c &= 4   \\
 					\therefore c &= 4 - a - b \\
							&= 4 - 1 \\
\therefore c &= 3 \\
\therefore T_n = n^2 + 3
	\end{aligned}\]

\[\begin{aligned}
	T_n &=  an^2 + bn + c \\
	\text{Second difference: } 2a &= 2 \\
														\therefore a &= 1 \\
	3a + b  &=  4 \\
 	b &=  4 - 3(1)  \\
 					\therefore b &= 1   \\
 	a + b + c &= 3   \\
 					\therefore c &= 3 - a - b \\
							&= 3 - 1 - 1 \\
\therefore c &= 1 \\
\therefore T_n &= n^2 + n + 1
	\end{aligned}\]

\[\begin{aligned}
	T_n &=  an^2 + bn + c \\
	\text{Second difference: } 2a &= 1 \\
														\therefore a &= \frac{1}{2} \\
	3a + b  &=  3 \\
 	b &=  3 - 3(\frac{1}{2})  \\
 					\therefore b &= \frac{3}{2}   \\
 	a + b + c &= 3   \\
 					\therefore c &= 3 - a - b \\
							&= 3 - \frac{1}{2} - \frac{3}{2} \\
\therefore c &= 1 \\
\therefore T_n &= \frac{1}{2}n^2 + \frac{3}{2}n + 1
	\end{aligned}\]

	\text{Let } T_2 &=   x \\
	\therefore T_2 - T_1 &=   x - 4 \\
	\text{And } T_3 - T_2 &=   34 - x \\
	\text{Second difference } &=  (T_3 - T_2) - (T_2 - T_1)  \\

\(T_n = an^2 + bn + c\)
----
\(d\)
----
\(D\)
----
\(a = \dfrac{D}{2}\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	T_n &=   an^2 + bn +c \\
	T_1 &=   a(1)^2 + b(1) +c \\
	    &=   a + b + c \\
	T_2 &=   a(2)^2 + b(2) +c \\
	    &=   4a + 2b + c\\
	T_3 &=   a(3)^2 + b(3) +c \\
	    &=   9a + 6b + c\\
	\text{First difference } d &=  T_2 - T_1 \\
					\therefore d	 &= (4a + 2b + c) - (a + b + c ) \\
					            	 &= 3a + b \\
					\therefore b &= d - 3a \\
	\text{Second difference } D &=    (T_3 - T_2) - (T_2 - T_1)\\
					\therefore D	 &= (5a + b) - (3a + b) \\
					            	 &= 2a \\
					\therefore a &= \dfrac{D}{2}
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\(b = d - \dfrac{3}{2}D\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
					  a &= \dfrac{D}{2} \\
					  b &= d - 3a \\
					\therefore b	&= d - 3 \left( \dfrac{D}{2}  \right) \\
		   		            	 &= d -  \dfrac{3}{2} D 
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\(c = T_1 - d + D\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	   T_1 &=   a + b + c \\
\therefore c &=   T_1 - a - b \\
					   &= T_1 - \left( \dfrac{D}{2} \right) -  \left( d -  \dfrac{3}{2}D \right) \\
					   &= T_1  -  \dfrac{D}{2}  - d + \dfrac{3}{2}D \\
						 &= T_1 - d + D
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\(T_n = \dfrac{D}{2}n^2 + \left(d - \dfrac{3}{2}D\right)n + \left(T_1 -d + D\right)\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
	   T_n &=   an^2 + bn +c \\
\therefore T_n  &=   \dfrac{D}{2}n^2 + \left( d - \dfrac{3}{2}D  \right)n + \left( T_1 - d + D \right) 
	\end{aligned}\]

\[\begin{aligned}
	QT &= \sqrt{ \left( x_2 - x_1 \right)^2 + \left( y_2 - y_1 \right)^2} \\
	 \sqrt{8}  &= \sqrt{ \left( p-4 \right)^2 + \left( 3-1\right)^2} \\
	\left( \sqrt{8} \right)^2 &=   \left( p-4 \right)^2 + \left( 2 \right)^2 \\
	 8  &=  p^2 - 8p + 16 + 4 \\
	 0  &=  p^2 - 8p + 16 + 4 - 8\\
	  &=  p^2 - 8p + 12 \\
	  &=   \left( p - 6 \right) \left( p - 2 \right)  \\
	 \therefore p  =  6  &\text{ or } p = 2
	\end{aligned}\]
----

\((3;-\frac{11}{4})\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
x  &= y - 5 \\ 
	x + 5 &= y   \\
	\therefore m_1 &= 1 \\
 m_2 &= \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1} \\ 
     &= \frac{-\frac{11}{4} -\frac{5}{4}}{3 + 1} \\
     &= \frac{-4}{4} \\
	\therefore m_2 &= -1 \\
 \therefore m_1 \times m_2&= -1 \times 1 \\
                        &= -1  
	\end{aligned}\]
----
\(\therefore\)

\[\begin{aligned}

	y &= 3x   \\
	\therefore m_1 &= 3 \\
3y + x &= 9 \\ 
	3y &= -x + 9  \\
	y &= -\frac{1}{3}x + 3  \\
	\therefore m_2 &= -\frac{1}{3} \\
 \therefore m_1 \times m_2&= -\frac{1}{3} \times 3 \\
                        &= -1  
	\end{aligned}\]

\(\therefore\)

     &= \frac{6}{-3} \\

 \therefore m_1 \times m_2&= -2 \times -2 \\
                        &\ne -1

\(\triangle ABC\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
BC &= \sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(3-2)^2 + (0-4)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(1)^2 + (4)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{1 + 16} \\
    &= \sqrt{17} \\
AB &= \sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(2+2)^2 + (4-3)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(4)^2 + (1)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{16 + 1} \\
    &= \sqrt{17} \\
    \therefore BC &= AB \\
\therefore \triangle ABC &\text{ is isosceles triangle } \\
AC &= \sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(3+2)^2 + (0-3)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(5)^2 + (-3)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{25+9} \\
    &= \sqrt{34} \\
 \text{And } BC^2 + AB^2 &= 17 + 17 \\
   &= 34 \\
   &= AC^2 \\
 \therefore \triangle ABC &\text{ is right-angled triangle}  
	\end{aligned}\]

\(NM = \frac{1}{2}CB\)
----
\[\begin{aligned}
    m_{NM}  &= \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1} \\
     &= \dfrac{1+\frac{1}{2}}{2+\frac{1}{2}} \\
      &= \dfrac{\frac{3}{2}}{\frac{5}{2}} \\
      &= \frac{3}{5} \\
    m_{CB}  &= \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1} \\
     &= \frac{-3+6}{5-0} \\
      &= \frac{3}{5} \\
      m_{NM} &= m_{CB} \\
 \therefore NM &\parallel CB \\
NM &= \sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(2+\frac{1}{2})^2 + (1+\frac{1}{2})^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(\frac{5}{2})^2 + (\frac{3}{2})^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{\frac{25}{4} + \frac{9}{4}} \\
    &= \sqrt{\frac{34}{4}} \\
    &= \frac{1}{2}\sqrt{34} \\
CB &= \sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(5-0)^2 + (-3+6)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{(5)^2 + (3)^2} \\
    &= \sqrt{25 + 9} \\
    &= \sqrt{34} \\
    \therefore NM &= \frac{1}{2}CB  
	\end{aligned}\]

\[\begin{aligned}

&= 36 +1 \\
\therefore & (0;37) \\

&= 4x^2 -36x + 37 \\
\therefore x & = \frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\
& = \frac{24 \pm \sqrt{(-24)^2 - 4(4)(37)}}{2(4)} \\
& = \frac{576 \pm \sqrt{576 - 592}}{8} \\
& = \frac{576 \pm \sqrt{-16}}{8} \\
\therefore &\text{ no real solution }
\end{aligned}\]

 &= 2(x^2 + 6x + 9) + 4x+12 + 2 \\
 &= 2x^2 + 12x + 18 + 4x+12 + 2 \\
 &= 2x^2 + 16x + 32 
\end{aligned}\]

 &= -x^2 - 2x - 1 + 1 \\
 &= -x^2 - 2x
\end{aligned}\]

\(f(x) = \frac{1}{x + 4} - 2\)
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
f(x) &= \frac{1}{x + 4} - 2  \\
\text{Let } x & = 0 \\
f(0) &= \frac{1}{4} - 2 \\
\therefore y_\text{int} &=(0;-1\frac{3}{4}) \\
\text{Let } y & = 0 \\
0 &= \frac{1}{x + 4} - 2  \\
2 &= \frac{1}{x + 4}    \\
2(x + 4) &= 1   \\
2x + 8 &= 1   \\
2x &= -7   \\
\therefore x &= -\frac{7}{2}  \\
\therefore x_\text{int} &= \left( -3\frac{1}{2}; 0 \right) 
\end{aligned}\]

\(g(x) = -\frac{5}{x} + 2\)
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
g(x) &= -\frac{5}{x} + 2   \\
\text{Let } x & = 0 \\
\therefore g(x) & \text{is undefined }   \\
\therefore \text{no } & x-\text{intercepts} \\
\text{Let } y & = 0 \\
0 &= -\frac{5}{x} + 2 \\
-2 &= -\frac{5}{x}     \\
2x &= 5  \\
\therefore x &= \frac{5}{2}   \\
\therefore x_\text{int} &= \left( \frac{5}{2} ; 0 \right)

-3x &= -1   \\
\therefore x &= \frac{1}{3}  \\

\end{aligned}\]

\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{Average gradient } &= \frac{f(3) - f(1)}{3 - 1} \\
&= \dfrac{-\frac{3}{3} - \left( -\frac{3}{1} \right)}{3-1} \\
&= \dfrac{-1 +3}{2} \\
&= \dfrac{2}{2} \\
&= 1
\end{aligned}\]

\((\frac{1}{2};-6)\)
----
\(x=1\)
----
\(x=3\)
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{Average gradient } &= \frac{f(a+h) - f(a)}{(a+h) - a} \\
&= \dfrac{-\frac{3}{a+h} - \left( -\frac{3}{a} \right)}{(a+h)-a} \\
&= \dfrac{-\frac{3}{a+h}  + \frac{3}{a}}{h} \\
&= \dfrac{\frac{-3(a) + 3(a+h)}{a(a+h)}}{h} \\
&= \dfrac{\frac{-3a + 3a+3h}{a^2+ah}}{h} \\
&= \dfrac{\frac{3h}{a^2+ah}}{h} \\
&= \frac{3h}{a^2+ah} \times \frac{1}{h} \\
&= \frac{3}{a^2+ah} \\
\therefore \text{At } (\frac{1}{2}; -6) \qquad a &= \frac{1}{2} \\
\therefore \text{And  }  \qquad h &= 0 \\
\therefore \text{Average gradient } &= \frac{3}{\left( \frac{1}{2} \right)^2+\frac{1}{2}(0)} \\
&= 3 \times \frac{4}{1} \\
&= 12
\end{aligned}\]
----
\((\frac{1}{2};-6)\)

\(h(x) = \frac{k}{x + p} + q\)

\[\begin{aligned} 
h(x) &=  \frac{k}{x + p} + q \\
\text{From graph: } \quad p = -2 \\
h(x) &=  \frac{k}{x + 2} + q \\
\text{Subst. } (0; -\frac{1}{2}) \quad -\frac{1}{2} &= \frac{k}{2} + q  \\
-1 &= k + 2q \ldots (1)\\
\text{Subst. } (1;0) \quad 0 &= \frac{k}{1 + 2} + q  \\
0 &= k + 3q \ldots (2)\\
(2) - (1): \qquad 1 &= 0 + q \\
\therefore q &= 1 \\
\text{and } k &= -3\\
\therefore h(x) &=  -\frac{3}{x + 2} + 1
\end{aligned}\]
----

 \text{subst. } (3;9) \quad 9 &=  a(3)^2 + b(3) \\
   9 &=  9a  + 3b  \\
   9 &=  9a  + 3(-6a)  \\
   9 &=  9a  -18a  \\
   9 &=  -9a  \\
   \therefore -1 &=  a  \\
   \therefore b &=  6   
\end{align}\]

    &= \frac{y^2 + x^2}{r^2} \\
    &= \frac{r^2}{r^2} \\
    &= 1
    \end{align}\]

    \tan^2 \theta \times \cos^2 \theta &= \left( \frac{\sin \theta}{\cos \theta} \right)^2 \times \cos^2 \theta \\
    &= \frac{\sin^2 \theta}{\cos^2 \theta} \times \cos^2 \theta \\
    &= \sin^2 \theta
    \end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
    \frac{1}{\cos^2 \theta} - \tan^2 \theta &= \frac{1}{\cos^2 \theta} - \left( \frac{\sin \theta}{\cos \theta} \right)^2 \\
    &= \frac{1}{\cos^2 \theta} - \frac{\sin^2 \theta}{\cos^2 \theta} \\
    &= \frac{1 - \sin^2 \theta}{\cos^2 \theta} \\
    &= \frac{\cos^2 \theta}{\cos^2 \theta} \\
    &= 1
    \end{align}\]

                                \text{LHS} &= \frac{1 - \sin \alpha}{\cos \alpha}  \\

                                \end{align}\]

\[\begin{align}
                                \text{LHS} &= \frac{1 - \sin^2 \alpha}{\cos \alpha(1 + \sin \alpha)} \\
                                &= \frac{\cos^2 \alpha}{\cos \alpha(1 + \sin \alpha)} \\
                                &= \frac{\cos \alpha}{1 + \sin \alpha} \\
                                &= \text{RHS}
                                \end{align}\]

----
\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{LHS } &= \dfrac{1+\sin \theta }{\cos\theta }\\
&=\dfrac{(1+\sin\theta)}{\cos\theta})\times \dfrac{(1-\sin\theta)}{1-\sin\theta}\\
&=\dfrac{1-\sin^2\theta}{\cos\theta(1-\sin\theta)} \\
&=\dfrac{\cos^2\theta }{\cos\theta(1-\sin\theta)} \\
&=\dfrac{\cos\theta}{(1-\sin\theta)} \\
&= \text{RHS} 
\end{aligned}\]

&=\sin^2\alpha+\cos^2\alpha-\tan^2\alpha \\
&=1 - \tan^2\alpha \\
&= \text{RHS}

\(\dfrac{1}{\cos\theta}-\dfrac{\cos\theta {\tan}^{2}\theta }{1}=\cos\theta\)
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{LHS } &= \dfrac{1}{\cos\theta}-\dfrac{\cos\theta \tan^2\theta}{1}\\
&=\dfrac{1-\cos^2\theta \times \tan^2\theta}{\cos\theta}\\
&=\dfrac{1-\cos^2\theta \times \dfrac{\sin^2\theta}{\cos^2\theta}}{\cos\theta}\\
&=\dfrac{1-\sin^2\theta}{\cos\theta}\\
&=\dfrac{\cos^2\theta}{\cos\theta}\\
&=\cos\theta\\
&= \text{RHS} 
\end{aligned}\]

\(\dfrac{2\sin\theta\cos\theta}{\sin\theta +\cos\theta }=\sin\theta +\cos\theta -\dfrac{1}{\sin\theta +\cos\theta }\)
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{RHS } &= \sin\theta+\cos\theta-\dfrac{1}{\sin\theta+\cos\theta} \\
&=\dfrac{\sin^2\theta+\sin\theta \cos\theta+\cos\theta \sin\theta+\cos^2\theta-1}{\sin\theta+\cos\theta} \\
&=\dfrac{1+2\sin\theta \cos\theta-1}{\sin\theta+\cos\theta} \\
&=\dfrac{2\sin\theta \cos\theta}{\sin\theta+\cos\theta} \\
&= \text{LHS} 
\end{aligned}\]

\(\left(\dfrac{\cos\beta}{\sin\beta }+\tan\beta \right) \cos\beta =\dfrac{1}{\sin\beta }\)

\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{ LHS} &=  \left ( \dfrac{\cos\beta}{\sin\beta}+\dfrac{\sin\beta}{\cos\beta} \right ) \\

\end{aligned}\]

\end{aligned}\]

\[\begin{aligned}

&=\dfrac{2 \sin \theta}{\sin \theta \cos \theta \cos \theta} \\
&=\dfrac{2}{\cos^2\theta} \\
\therefore \text{LHS } &= \text{RHS } 
\end{aligned}\]

\(\dfrac{(1 + \tan^2 \alpha) \cos \alpha}{(1 - \tan \alpha)} = \dfrac{1}{\cos \alpha - \sin \alpha}\)
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{ LHS} &= \dfrac{(1 + \tan^2 \alpha) \cos \alpha}{(1 - \tan \alpha)} \\
&= \dfrac{\left (1+\frac{\sin^2\alpha}{\cos^2\alpha}  \right )\cos\alpha}{\left ( 1-\frac{\sin\alpha}{\cos\alpha} \right )} \\
&=\dfrac{\left ( \frac{\cos^2\alpha+\sin^2\alpha}{\cos^2\alpha} \right )\cos\alpha}{\frac{\cos\alpha-\sin\alpha}{\cos\alpha}}\\
&=\dfrac{1}{\cos\alpha}\times \frac{\cos\alpha}{\cos\alpha-\sin\alpha} \\
&=\dfrac{1}{\cos\alpha-\sin\alpha} \\
&= \text{RHS } 
\end{aligned}\]

                    \therefore CF &= \ldots \times \sin \hat{B}
                    \end{align}\]

\(\triangle CAF\)
----
\[\begin{align}
                    \frac{CF}{15} &= \ldots    \\
                    \therefore CF &= 15 \times \ldots
                    \end{align}\]
----
\[\begin{align}
                    CF &=  15 \times \ldots   \\
                    \text{and } CF &= \ldots \times \sin \hat{B} \\
                    \therefore  15 \times \ldots &= \ldots \times \sin \hat{B}  \\
                    \therefore \sin \hat{B} &= \ldots \ldots \ldots \\
                    \therefore \hat{B} &= \ldots
                    \end{align}\]

\[\begin{align*}
    a^2 &= (c-d)^2 + h^2 \\
\therefore h^2 &= a^2 - (c-d)^2 \\
    \text{And } b^2 &= d^2 + h^2 \\
\therefore h^2 &= b^2  - d^2 \\
  \therefore b^2 - d^2 &= a^2 - (c-d)^2 \\
  a^2 &= b^2 + (c^2 - 2cd + d^2) - d^2 \\
  &= b^2 + c^2 - 2cd
\end{align*}\]

  \text{In } \triangle ABE, \quad \frac{x}{EB}    &= \cos \theta \\
\therefore EB    &= \frac{x}{\cos \theta} \\
  \text{In } \triangle BDC, \quad \frac{DB}{\sin \alpha}    &= \frac{x}{\sin \beta} \\
\therefore DB     &= \frac{x \sin \alpha }{\sin \beta} \\
                \therefore \text{Area} \triangle BED &= \frac{1}{2}(BE)(BD)\sin (\beta - \theta)\\
                    &= \frac{1}{2} \times \frac{x}{\cos \theta} \times \frac{x \sin \alpha }{\sin \beta} \times \sin (\beta - \theta)\\
            &=  \frac{x^2 \sin \alpha \sin (\beta - \theta) }{2 \cos \theta \sin \beta}
\end{align}\]

\(\dfrac{1}{(\cos x - 1)(\cos x + 1)} = \dfrac{-1}{\tan^2x \cos^2x}\)
----
\[\begin{align}
\text{ RHS  }&=\frac{-1}{\frac{\sin^2x}{\cos^2x}\dottimes\frac{\cos^2x}{1}} \\
&=\frac{-1}{\sin^2x} \\
\text{ LHS  } &=\frac{1}{\cos^2x-1} \\
&=\frac{1}{-(1-\cos^2x)} \\
&=-\frac{1}{\sin^2x} \\
&=\text{ RHS  }
\end{align}\]

\((1 - \tan \alpha) \cos \alpha = \sin(90 + \alpha) + \cos(90 + \alpha)\)
----
\[\begin{align}
    \text{LHS} &= (1 - \frac{\sin \alpha}{\cos \alpha}) . \cos \alpha \\
    &= (\frac{\cos \alpha - \sin \alpha}{\cos \alpha} ) \cos \alpha \\
    &= \cos \alpha - \sin \alpha \\
    \text{RHS} &= \cos (-\alpha) + \sin (-\alpha) \\
    &= \cos \alpha - \sin \alpha \\
    &= \text{LHS}
  \end{align}\]
----
\(\tan y + \dfrac{1}{\tan y} = \dfrac{1}{\cos^2y \tan y}\)
----
\[\begin{align}
    \text{LHS} &= \frac{\sin y}{\cos y} + \frac{1}{\frac{1}{\sin y}{\cos y}}\\
    &= \frac{\sin y}{\cos y} + \frac{\cos y}{\sin y}\\
    &= \frac{\sin^2 y + \cos^2 y}{\cos y . \sin y}\\
    &= \frac{1}{\cos y . \sin y}\\
    \text{RHS} &= \frac{1}{\cos^2 y \frac{\sin y}{\cos y}}\\
    &= \frac{\cos y}{\cos^2 y . \sin y}\\
    &= \frac{1}{\cos y \sin y}\\
    &= \text{LHS}
  \end{align}\]

  =& 5^2 \times 2 (lh + lb + bh) \\

\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{Volume }&=k \times k\times k \\
&=k^3 \\
\text{New volume }&=k\times k\times 3k \\
&=3k^3
\end{aligned}\]
----
\[\begin{aligned} 
\text{Surface area } &= 6\times k^2 \\
&=6k^2 \\
\text{Surface area }&= 6\times (3k)^2 \\
&=54k^2
\end{aligned}\]

&=27k^3
\end{aligned}\]

\(\triangle OPB\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
      OA^2 &= OP^2 + AP^2 & \text{(Pythagoras)} \\
      OB^2 &= OP^2 + BP^2 & \text{(Pythagoras)}
      \end{array}\]
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
      OA  &= OB & \text{(equal radii)} \\
      \therefore AP^2 &= BP^2 & \\
      \therefore AP &= BP &
      \end{array}\]
----

\(\triangle OPA\)
----
\(\triangle OPB\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
      O\hat{P}A &= O\hat{P}B & (\text{given } OP \perp AB) \\
      OA &= OB & \text{(equal radii)} \\
      OP &= OP & \text{(common side)}  \\
      \therefore \triangle OPA & \equiv  \triangle OPB & \text{(RHS)}  \\
      \therefore AP &= PB &
      \end{array}\]

\[\begin{array}{rll}
        PQ &= 4   & (\perp \text{ from centre bisects chord}) \\
        OP^2 &= OQ^2 + QP^2 & (\text{Pythagoras}) \\
        5^2 &= x^2 + 4^2   & \\
        \therefore x^2 &= 25 - 16  & \\
        x^2 &= 9  & \\
        x &= 3 &
        \end{array}\]
----
\(x = 3\)

        PR &= 10   & (\perp \text{ given }) \\
        \therefore         PQ &= 5   & (\perp \text{ from centre bisects chord}) \\
        OP^2 &= OQ^2 + QP^2 & (\text{Pythagoras}) \\
        x^2 &= 4^2 + 5^2   & \\
        \therefore x^2 &= 25 + 16  & \\
        x^2 &= 41  & \\
        x &= \sqrt{41} &
        \end{array}\]
----
\(x=\sqrt{41}\)

\(A\hat{O}Q = \hat{O}_1\)
----
\(B\hat{O}Q = \hat{O}_2\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
      \hat{O}_1&= A\hat{P}O  + P\hat{A}O    & (\text{ext. } \angle \triangle = \text{sum int. opp. } \angle \text{s} ) \\
      \text{and } A\hat{P}O &=  P\hat{A}O     & (\text{equal radii, isosceles } \triangle APO)\\
      \therefore \hat{O}_1&= A\hat{P}O  +  A\hat{P}O   &  \\
        \hat{O}_1&= 2A\hat{P}O     &  
\end{array}\]
----
\(\hat{O}_2 = 2B\hat{P}O\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
     A\hat{O}B  &= \hat{O}_1 + \hat{O}_2  &  \\
                         &= 2A\hat{P}O  + 2B\hat{P}O    &  \\
                         &= 2(A\hat{P}O  + B\hat{P}O)    &  \\
  \therefore A\hat{O}B &= 2(A\hat{P}B)    &  
\end{array}\]
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
     A\hat{O}B  &= \hat{O}_2 - \hat{O}_1  &  \\
                         &= 2B\hat{P}O  - 2A\hat{P}O    &  \\
                         &= 2(B\hat{P}O  - A\hat{P}O)    &  \\
  \therefore A\hat{O}B &= 2(A\hat{P}B)    &  
\end{array}\]

\(a\)

----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
          AB = AF&= a  & (\text{tangents from } A) \\
          EF = ED&= c  & (\text{tangents from } E) \\
          CB = CD&= b  & (\text{tangents from } C) \\
          \therefore AE = a + c &= 5 & \\
          \text{and } AC = a + b &= 8 & \\
          \text{and } CE = b + c &= 9 &
  \end{array}\]
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
        a + c &= 5 & \ldots (1)\\
        a + b &= 8 & \ldots (2)\\
        b + c &= 9 & \ldots (3)
  \end{array}\]
----
\((1)\)
----
\((2)\)
----
\((3)\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
        (2) - (1) \quad b-c &= 8-5 & \\
        &= 3 & \\
        \therefore b &= c + 3 & \\
        \text{Substitute into } (3) \quad c + 3 + c &= 9 & \\
        2c &= 6 & \\
        c &= 3 & \\
        \therefore a &= 2 & \\
        \text{ and } b &= 6 &
  \end{array}\]

\(\hat{A}_2 = \hat{B}_2\)
----
\(PAL\)
----
\(ABC\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
        \hat{A}_1 &=  A\hat{C}B  & (\text{alt. angles}, AP \parallel BC) \\
                A\hat{C}B &=  A\hat{B}C & (\angle \text{s opp. equal sides }, AB = AC) \\
        \therefore \hat{A}_1  &=   A\hat{B}C  &   \\
        \text{Therefore } PAL &  \text{is a tangent to circle }  ABC   & (\angle\text{ between line chord} = \angle\text{ in alt. seg.})
     \end{array}\]
----
\(AB\)
----
\(ADP\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
        \hat{A}_2 &=  \hat{B}_2  & (\text{ given }) \\
      \text{And } A\hat{P}B  &=    \hat{B}_2  &   (\text{alt. angles}, AP \parallel BC) \\
        \text{Therefore } A\hat{P}B &=  \hat{A}_2  ABC   &  \\
        \text{Therefore } AB &  \text{is a tangent to circle }  ADP   & (\angle\text{ between line chord} = \angle\text{ in alt. seg.})
     \end{array}\]

\(B\hat{F}C = B\hat{C}F\)

\[\begin{array}{rll}
               B\hat{C}F &= C\hat{E}O & (\text{tangent-chord}) \\
               C\hat{E}O &= B\hat{F}C & (\text{ext. } \angle \text{ cyclic quad. } CFOE) \\
               \therefore B\hat{F}C &= B\hat{C}F \\
               \therefore FB &= BC & (\triangle BFC \text{ isosceles})
       \end{array}\]

\(A\hat{O}C = 2 B\hat{F}C\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
              A\hat{O}C &= 2 A\hat{E}C & (\angle \text{ at centre } = 2 \angle \text{ at circum.}) \\
              \text{and } A\hat{E}C &= B\hat{F}C    & (\text{ext. } \angle \text{ cyclic quad. } CFOE)  \\
              \therefore A\hat{O}C &= 2 B\hat{F}C
      \end{array}\]

\(F\hat{E}A = \hat{B}\)
----
\(FADE\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
              F\hat{D}C &= D\hat{C}B &  (\text{alt. } \angle\text{s } FD \parallel CB) \\
              \text{and } D\hat{C}B  &= C\hat{A}E    &  (\text{tangent-chord})   \\
              \therefore F\hat{D}C &= C\hat{A}E \\
              \therefore FADE & \text{is a cyclic quad.}   & (\angle \text{s in same seg.})
      \end{array}\]
----
\(F\hat{E}A = \hat{B}\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
              F\hat{D}A &= \hat{B} & (\text{corresp. } \angle\text{s } FD \parallel CB) \\
              \text{and } F\hat{E}A  &= F\hat{D}A    &  (\angle \text{s same seg.\@ cyclic quad.\@ } FADE)   \\
              \therefore F\hat{E}A &= \hat{B}
      \end{array}\]

\(C\hat{E}D = 2 C\hat{B}A\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
    C\hat{E}D &= C\hat{B}D& (\angle\text{'s on chord } CD)\\
    \text{But } C\hat{B}A &= D\hat{B}A & (\triangle CBP \equiv \triangle DBP)\\
    \therefore C\hat{E}D &= 2 C\hat{B}A
  \end{array}\]
----
\(A\hat{B}D = \frac{1}{2} C\hat{O}A\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
    D\hat{B}A &= C\hat{B}A & (\triangle CBP \equiv \triangle DBP)\\
    C\hat{B}A &=  \frac{1}{2}  C\hat{O}A & (\angle\text{'s at centre and circumference on arc } AC)\\
    \therefore A\hat{B}D &= \frac{1}{2} C\hat{O}A &
  \end{array}\]

\[\begin{array}{rll}
    \text{In } &\triangle QOS,  & \\
    QO^2 &=  OS^2 + QS^2 & ( \text{Pythagoras }) \\
    x^2 &=  (x-9)^2 + 15^2 &  \\
    x^2 &=  x^2 - 18x + 81  + 225 &  \\
    \therefore 18x &=   306  &  \\
    \therefore x &=   17  &  
  \end{array}\]

\(AB = AC\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
       C\hat{P}Q &= A\hat{B}C & ( \text{ ext. angle of cyclic quad. } ) \\
       B\hat{C}P &= C\hat{P}Q + C\hat{Q}P   &  (  \text{ ext. angle of } \triangle )  \\
       A\hat{C}P &=  C\hat{Q}P   &  ( \text{ tangent-chord } )  \\
                \therefore  B\hat{C}A &=  C\hat{P}Q  &   \\
                \therefore    &=  A\hat{B}C  &   \\
                \therefore   AB  &= AC & \text{ angles opp. equal sides}
    \end{array}\]

\(Q\hat{R}P = y\)

\(T\hat{V}S = 2 Q\hat{R}S\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
       \text{In }   &\triangle VQS,    &  \\
                VQ &= VS    &  ( \text{ tangents from same pt. } ) \\
        \therefore V\hat{S}Q  &= V\hat{Q}S = x  &  (\angle \text{s opp. equal sides  })  \\
                \therefore T\hat{V}S &= x + x   & (\text{ext. angle of } \triangle ) \\
         &= 2x  &  \\
                    \text{And } Q\hat{R}S  &= Q\hat{P}S = x &  (\angle \text{ same seg. })  \\
                \therefore T\hat{V}S &= 2Q\hat{R}S   &
    \end{array}\]
----
\(QVSW\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
                T\hat{V}S &= 2Q\hat{R}S    &  ( \text{ proven }  )\\
                        V\hat{Q}S  &= Q\hat{P}S    &  ( \text{ tangent-chord }  )\\
                         Q\hat{P}S    &= P\hat{S}R = x    &  ( \text{ alt. } \angle, PQ \parallel RT  )\\
                    \text{And } Q\hat{W}S  &= 2Q\hat{R}S  &  (\angle \text{ ext. angle of } \triangle WSR )  \\
                    \therefore T\hat{V}S &= Q\hat{W}S    &= 2x  \\
                 \therefore QVSW &= \text{ is cyclic quad. }   &   \text{ext. angle = int. opp. angle }
    \end{array}\]
----
\(Q\hat{P}S + \hat{T} = P\hat{R}T\)
----
\[\begin{array}{rll}
                        \hat{Q} &= Q\hat{R}P = y   &  ( \text{ tangent-chord }  )\\
                \hat{Q} &= \hat{T} = y    &  ( \text{ alt. } \angle, PQ \parallel RT  )\\
                         P\hat{R}T    &= x + y    &   \\
                    \text{And } Q\hat{P}S  &= x  &  (\angle \text{ proven }  )  \\
                    \therefore Q\hat{P}S + \hat{T} &= x + y   &= P\hat{R}T
    \end{array}\]
----
\(W\)

\[\begin{array}{rll}
                 Q\hat{R}S  &= x    &  ( \text{ proven }  )\\
                        Q\hat{W}S  &= 2x    &  ( \text{ proven }  )\\
                 \therefore W &= \text{ is circle centre. }   &   (\angle \text{ centre = 2 angle at circum. }
    \end{array}\]

    \end{array}\]

                     \hat{A}   &= \hat{C}_1    &   ( \text{ alt. angles }, AE \parallel BC ) \\
                        \therefore \hat{A}  &= \hat{E}    &    \\
                 \therefore  AC &= CE  &   (\angle \text{ angles opp. equal sides } \\
                   BF &= CE  &   (\angle \text{ opp. sides parm. =} \\
                   \therefore AC &= BF  &
    \end{array}\]
